## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress generally increases with strain (elastic/hardening behavior) and decreases with increasing temperature (thermal softening). Classical constitutive models from plasticity and creep theory govern these relationships.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at small strains)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening in plasticity)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (strain hardening with temperature dependence)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type temperature dependence with hardening)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Power-law creep form: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with power-law plastic term)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * (c2 * T)) * sinh(c3 * epsilon) (hyperbolic sine creep model)
- Ludwik with thermal: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 * exp(c4 * T) (yield stress plus hardening, both temperature-dependent)
- Bilinear with softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T + c3 * T**2) (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Johnson-Cook full thermal: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - ((T - c3) * c4)**c5) (homologous temperature softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (Tm - T)**c or exp(-c*T) representing decreasing flow stress with temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form where stress approaches a saturation value at large strains
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 (typically c ≈ 0.1-0.5 for metals), representing diminishing hardening rate
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield stress independent of strain, sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Competing elastic and plastic regimes → sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and nonlinear term (c1*epsilon**c2) representing transition from elastic to plastic
- Homologous temperature scaling → temperature appears as (T - T_ref)*c or (Tmelt - T)*c rather than absolute T, reflecting material-specific reference points
- Thermally activated deformation → sinh(c*epsilon) or asinh(c*sigma) forms from thermal activation theory of dislocation motion
- Coupled strain-temperature interaction → product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicating that hardening rate depends on temperature

Key structural features:
- `T*epsilon` (linear)
- `epsilon` (linear)
- `epsilon**3` 
- `T*sin(epsilon)`
- `sin(epsilon)`

Now I'll check candidates for ones that can produce these terms.

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*sin(T*c5 + c6) + c7 + c8*epsilon`

This has `T*c1*epsilon` ✓, `c2*epsilon**c3` (set c3=3) ✓, `c8*epsilon` ✓, but `c4*sin(T*c5 + c6)` cannot produce `T*sin(epsilon)`. ✗

Setting c2=1: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + c3*sin(T*c4+c5) + c6 + c7*epsilon`. Can't get `epsilon**3` or `T*sin(epsilon)`. ✗

**Candidate 65:** `c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*sin(c4*epsilon + c5) + c6*(T*c7)**c8 + c9*epsilon**c2*(T*c7)**c8`

Setting c8=1: `c6*c7*T + c9*c7*T*epsilon**c2 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*sin(c4*epsilon+c5) + c0`

If c2=1: `c9*c7*T*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c6*c7*T + c3*sin(c4*epsilon+c5) + c0`
This gives T*epsilon ✓, epsilon ✓, T ✗ (GT has no standalone T term unless it cancels), sin(c4*epsilon+c5) but NOT T*sin(epsilon), and no epsilon**3. ✗

**Candidate 64:** `T*c0 + T*c1*(c2+epsilon)**c3 + c4 + c5*epsilon**5 + c6*epsilon**4 + c7*exp(T*c8) + c9*epsilon*exp(T*c8)`

If c3=1: `T*c0 + T*c1*c2 + T*c1*epsilon + c4 + ...` No sin term. ✗

Looking more carefully, none of the candidates contain `T*sin(epsilon)` as a producible structure. The GT requires both `T*sin(epsilon)` and `sin(epsilon)` terms. The only way to get `T*sin(epsilon)` is through explicit `T*sin(...)` structure.

**GT:** `99.72829794207104*epsilon*(-0.08976441603442807*(T - 330.599841780566) + 1) + 4.818532892851478*epsilon**3 + 5.41673901332906*(T - 330.599841780566)*sin(epsilon)`

- First term: `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*(T - 330.6) + 1)` = `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 0.08976...*330.6 + 1)` = `-8.952...*T*epsilon + 99.728...*epsilon*(0.08976*330.6 + 1)`

  Wait, let me recalculate: `0.08976*330.6 ≈ 29.674`, so the constant part is `99.728*(29.674+1) = 99.728*30.674 ≈ 3059.5` times epsilon... Let me just keep it symbolic.

**GT expanded:**
- `c0*c1*c2*epsilon - c0*c1*T*epsilon + c0*c3*epsilon + c4*epsilon^c5 + c6*T*sin(epsilon) - c6*c7*sin(epsilon)`

With numerical values:
- `T*epsilon` term: `-99.728*0.08976*T*epsilon + ...` = `-8.952*T*epsilon`
- `epsilon` term: `99.728*(0.08976*330.6 + 1)*epsilon` = `99.728*30.674*epsilon ≈ 3059.5*epsilon`
- `epsilon^3` term: `4.8185*epsilon^3`
- `T*sin(epsilon)` term: `5.4167*T*sin(epsilon)`
- `sin(epsilon)` term: `-5.4167*330.6*sin(epsilon) ≈ -1790.8*sin(epsilon)`

So GT = **a*T*epsilon + b*epsilon + c*epsilon^3 + d*T*sin(epsilon) + e*sin(epsilon)**

The basis functions are: `T*epsilon`, `epsilon`, `epsilon^3`, `T*sin(epsilon)`, `sin(epsilon)`.

1. Must have `T*epsilon` term
2. Must have `epsilon` term
3. Must have `epsilon^3` term
4. Must have `T*sin(epsilon)` term
5. Must have `sin(epsilon)` term
6. Must NOT require any other linearly independent basis functions

Let me check candidates systematically. Most candidates contain `exp(T*c)`, `log(T*c+1)`, `sqrt(T)`, `T^c`, `epsilon^4`, `epsilon^5`, `epsilon^2`, etc. These are linearly independent from the GT basis functions and cannot be zeroed out without losing needed terms.

None of the candidates appear to have a `T*sin(epsilon)` term. Without this term, no candidate can match the GT since `T*sin(epsilon)` is linearly independent from all other basis functions present.
